Kalt</div><div class="line" id="LC2">Request for Comments: 2812                                    April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC3">Updates: 1459</div><div class="line" id="LC4">Category: Informational</div><div class="line" id="LC5">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC6">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC7">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol</div><div class="line" id="LC8">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC9">Status of this Memo</div><div class="line" id="LC10">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC11">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This memo provides information for the Internet community.  It does</div><div class="line" id="LC12">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not specify an Internet standard of any kind.  Distribution of this</div><div class="line" id="LC13">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;memo is unlimited.</div><div class="line" id="LC14">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC15">Copyright Notice</div><div class="line" id="LC16">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC17">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Copyright (C) The Internet Society (2000).  All Rights Reserved.</div><div class="line" id="LC18">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC19">IESG NOTE:</div><div class="line" id="LC20">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC21">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The IRC protocol itself enables several possibilities of transferring</div><div class="line" id="LC22">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;data between clients, and just like with other transfer mechanisms</div><div class="line" id="LC23">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like email, the receiver of the data has to be careful about how the</div><div class="line" id="LC24">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;data is handled. For more information on security issues with the IRC</div><div class="line" id="LC25">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;protocol, see for example http://www.irchelp.org/irchelp/security/.</div><div class="line" id="LC26">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC27">Abstract</div><div class="line" id="LC28">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC29">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The IRC (Internet Relay Chat) protocol is for use with text based</div><div class="line" id="LC30">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;conferencing; the simplest client being any socket program capable of</div><div class="line" id="LC31">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;connecting to the server.</div><div class="line" id="LC32">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC33">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This document defines the Client Protocol, and assumes that the</div><div class="line" id="LC34">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;reader is familiar with the IRC Architecture [IRC-ARCH].</div><div class="line" id="LC35">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC36">Table of Contents</div><div class="line" id="LC37">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC38">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1.  Labels .....................................................   3</div><div class="line" id="LC39">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1.1  Servers ................................................   3</div><div class="line" id="LC40">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1.2  Clients ................................................   3</div><div class="line" id="LC41">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1.2.1  Users .............................................   4</div><div class="line" id="LC42">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1.2.1.1  Operators ....................................   4</div><div class="line" id="LC43">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1.2.2  Services ..........................................   4</div><div class="line" id="LC44">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1.3  Channels ...............................................   4</div><div class="line" id="LC45">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2.  The IRC Client Specification ...............................   5</div><div class="line" id="LC46">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2.1  Overview ...............................................   5</div><div class="line" id="LC47">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2.2  Character codes ........................................   5</div><div class="line" id="LC48">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2.3  Messages ...............................................   5</div><div class="line" id="LC49">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC50">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC51">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC52">Kalt                         Informational                      [Page 1]</div><div class="line" id="LC53">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC54">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC55">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC56">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC57">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2.3.1  Message format in Augmented BNF ...................   6</div><div class="line" id="LC58">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2.4  Numeric replies ........................................   8</div><div class="line" id="LC59">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2.5  Wildcard expressions ...................................   9</div><div class="line" id="LC60">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3. Optional features ..........................................  38</div><div class="line" id="LC114">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.1  Away ...................................................  38</div><div class="line" id="LC115">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.2  Rehash message .........................................  39</div><div class="line" id="LC116">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.3  Die message ............................................  39</div><div class="line" id="LC117">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.4  Restart message ........................................  40</div><div class="line" id="LC118">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.5  Summon message .........................................  40</div><div class="line" id="LC119">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.6  Users ..................................................  41</div><div class="line" id="LC120">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.7  Operwall message .......................................  41</div><div class="line" id="LC121">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.8  Userhost message .......................................  42</div><div class="line" id="LC122">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.9  Ison message ...........................................  42</div><div class="line" id="LC123">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;5.  Replies ....................................................  43</div><div class="line" id="LC124">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;5.1  Command responses ......................................  43</div><div class="line" id="LC125">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;5.2  Error Replies ..........................................  53</div><div class="line" id="LC126">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;5.3  Reserved numerics ......................................  59</div><div class="line" id="LC127">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.  Current implementations ....................................  60</div><div class="line" id="LC128">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;7.  Current problems ...........................................  60</div><div class="line" id="LC129">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;7.1  Nicknames ..............................................  60</div><div class="line" id="LC130">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;7.2  Limitation of wildcards ................................  61</div><div class="line" id="LC131">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;7.3  Security considerations ................................  61</div><div class="line" id="LC132">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;8.  Current support and availability ...........................  61</div><div class="line" id="LC133">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;9.  Acknowledgements ...........................................  61</div><div class="line" id="LC134">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;10.  References ................................................  62</div><div class="line" id="LC135">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;11.  Author&#39;s Address ..........................................  62</div><div class="line" id="LC136">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;12.  Full Copyright Statement ..................................  63</div><div class="line" id="LC137">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC138">1. Labels</div><div class="line" id="LC139">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC140">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This section defines the identifiers used for the various components</div><div class="line" id="LC141">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of the IRC protocol.</div><div class="line" id="LC142">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC143">1.1 Servers</div><div class="line" id="LC144">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC145">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Servers are uniquely identified by their name, which has a maximum</div><div class="line" id="LC146">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;length of sixty three (63) characters.  See the protocol grammar</div><div class="line" id="LC147">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;rules (section 2.3.1) for what may and may not be used in a server</div><div class="line" id="LC148">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;name.</div><div class="line" id="LC149">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC150">1.2 Clients</div><div class="line" id="LC151">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC152">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For each client all servers MUST have the following information: a</div><div class="line" id="LC153">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;netwide unique identifier (whose format depends on the type of</div><div class="line" id="LC154">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;client) and the server which introduced the client.</div><div class="line" id="LC155">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC156">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC157">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC158">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC159">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC160">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC161">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC162">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC163">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC164">Kalt                         Informational                      [Page 3]</div><div class="line" id="LC165">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC166">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC167">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC168">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC169">1.2.1 Users</div><div class="line" id="LC170">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC171">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Each user is distinguished from other users by a unique nickname</div><div class="line" id="LC172">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;having a maximum length of nine (9) characters.  See the protocol</div><div class="line" id="LC173">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;grammar rules (section 2.3.1) for what may and may not be used in a</div><div class="line" id="LC174">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nickname.</div><div class="line" id="LC175">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC176">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;While the maximum length is limited to nine characters, clients</div><div class="line" id="LC177">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;SHOULD accept longer strings as they may become used in future</div><div class="line" id="LC178">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;evolutions of the protocol.</div><div class="line" id="LC179">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC180">1.2.1.1 Operators</div><div class="line" id="LC181">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC182">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To allow a reasonable amount of order to be kept within the IRC</div><div class="line" id="LC183">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;network, a special class of users (operators) is allowed to perform</div><div class="line" id="LC184">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;general maintenance functions on the network.  Although the powers</div><div class="line" id="LC185">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;granted to an operator can be considered as &#39;dangerous&#39;, they are</div><div class="line" id="LC186">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nonetheless often necessary.  Operators SHOULD be able to perform</div><div class="line" id="LC187">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;basic network tasks such as disconnecting and reconnecting servers as</div><div class="line" id="LC188">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;needed.  In recognition of this need, the protocol discussed herein</div><div class="line" id="LC189">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;provides for operators only to be able to perform such functions.</div><div class="line" id="LC190">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;See sections 3.1.8 (SQUIT) and 3.4.7 (CONNECT).</div><div class="line" id="LC191">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC192">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A more controversial power of operators is the ability to remove a</div><div class="line" id="LC193">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;user from the connected network by &#39;force&#39;, i.e., operators are able</div><div class="line" id="LC194">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to close the connection between any client and server.  The</div><div class="line" id="LC195">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;justification for this is very delicate since its abuse is both</div><div class="line" id="LC196">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;destructive and annoying, and its benefits close to inexistent.  For</div><div class="line" id="LC197">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;further details on this type of action, see section 3.7.1 (KILL).</div><div class="line" id="LC198">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC199">1.2.2 Services</div><div class="line" id="LC200">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC201">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Each service is distinguished from other services by a service name</div><div class="line" id="LC202">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;composed of a nickname and a server name.  As for users, the nickname</div><div class="line" id="LC203">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;has a maximum length of nine (9) characters.  See the protocol</div><div class="line" id="LC204">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;grammar rules (section 2.3.1) for what may and may not be used in a</div><div class="line" id="LC205">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nickname.</div><div class="line" id="LC206">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC207">1.3 Channels</div><div class="line" id="LC208">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC209">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Channels names are strings (beginning with a &#39;&amp;&#39;, &#39;#&#39;, &#39;+&#39; or &#39;!&#39;</div><div class="line" id="LC210">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;character) of length up to fifty (50) characters.  Apart from the</div><div class="line" id="LC211">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;requirement that the first character is either &#39;&amp;&#39;, &#39;#&#39;, &#39;+&#39; or &#39;!&#39;,</div><div class="line" id="LC212">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the only restriction on a channel name is that it SHALL NOT contain</div><div class="line" id="LC213">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;any spaces (&#39; &#39;), a control G (^G or ASCII 7), a comma (&#39;,&#39;).  Space</div><div class="line" id="LC214">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is used as parameter separator and command is used as a list item</div><div class="line" id="LC215">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;separator by the protocol).  A colon (&#39;:&#39;) can also be used as a</div><div class="line" id="LC216">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;delimiter for the channel mask.  Channel names are case insensitive.</div><div class="line" id="LC217">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC218">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC219">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC220">Kalt                         Informational                      [Page 4]</div><div class="line" id="LC221">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC222">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC223">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC224">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC225">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;See the protocol grammar rules (section 2.3.1) for the exact syntax</div><div class="line" id="LC226">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of a channel name.</div><div class="line" id="LC227">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC228">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Each prefix characterizes a different channel type.  The definition</div><div class="line" id="LC229">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of the channel types is not relevant to the client-server protocol</div><div class="line" id="LC230">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thus it is beyond the scope of this document.  More details can</div><div class="line" id="LC231">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be found in &quot;Internet Relay Chat: Channel Management&quot; [IRC-CHAN].</div><div class="line" id="LC232">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC233">2. The IRC Client Specification</div><div class="line" id="LC234">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC235">2.1 Overview</div><div class="line" id="LC236">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC237">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The protocol as described herein is for use only with client to</div><div class="line" id="LC238">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;server connections when the client registers as a user.</div><div class="line" id="LC239">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC240">2.2 Character codes</div><div class="line" id="LC241">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC242">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;No specific character set is specified. The protocol is based on a</div><div class="line" id="LC243">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;set of codes which are composed of eight (8) bits, making up an</div><div class="line" id="LC244">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;octet.  Each message may be composed of any number of these octets;</div><div class="line" id="LC245">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;however, some octet values are used for control codes, which act as</div><div class="line" id="LC246">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;message delimiters.</div><div class="line" id="LC247">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC248">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Regardless of being an 8-bit protocol, the delimiters and keywords</div><div class="line" id="LC249">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are such that protocol is mostly usable from US-ASCII terminal and a</div><div class="line" id="LC250">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;telnet connection.</div><div class="line" id="LC251">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC252">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Because of IRC&#39;s Scandinavian origin, the characters {}|^ are</div><div class="line" id="LC253">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;considered to be the lower case equivalents of the characters []\~,</div><div class="line" id="LC254">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;respectively. This is a critical issue when determining the</div><div class="line" id="LC255">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;equivalence of two nicknames or channel names.</div><div class="line" id="LC256">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC257">2.3 Messages</div><div class="line" id="LC258">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC259">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Servers and clients send each other messages, which may or may not</div><div class="line" id="LC260">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;generate a reply.  If the message contains a valid command, as</div><div class="line" id="LC261">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;described in later sections, the client should expect a reply as</div><div class="line" id="LC262">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;specified but it is not advised to wait forever for the reply; client</div><div class="line" id="LC263">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to server and server to server communication is essentially</div><div class="line" id="LC264">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;asynchronous by nature.</div><div class="line" id="LC265">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC266">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Each IRC message may consist of up to three main parts: the prefix</div><div class="line" id="LC267">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(OPTIONAL), the command, and the command parameters (maximum of</div><div class="line" id="LC268">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fifteen (15)).  The prefix, command, and all parameters are separated</div><div class="line" id="LC269">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by one ASCII space character (0x20) each.</div><div class="line" id="LC270">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC271">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC272">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC273">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC274">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC275">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC276">Kalt                         Informational                      [Page 5]</div><div class="line" id="LC277">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC278">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC279">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC280">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC281">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The presence of a prefix is indicated with a single leading ASCII</div><div class="line" id="LC282">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;colon character (&#39;:&#39;, 0x3b), which MUST be the first character of the</div><div class="line" id="LC283">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;message itself.  There MUST be NO gap (whitespace) between the colon</div><div class="line" id="LC284">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and the prefix.  The prefix is used by servers to indicate the true</div><div class="line" id="LC285">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;origin of the message.  If the prefix is missing from the message, it</div><div class="line" id="LC286">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is assumed to have originated from the connection from which it was</div><div class="line" id="LC287">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;received from.  Clients SHOULD NOT use a prefix when sending a</div><div class="line" id="LC288">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;message; if they use one, the only valid prefix is the registered</div><div class="line" id="LC289">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nickname associated with the client.</div><div class="line" id="LC290">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC291">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The command MUST either be a valid IRC command or a three (3) digit</div><div class="line" id="LC292">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;number represented in ASCII text.</div><div class="line" id="LC293">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC294">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;IRC messages are always lines of characters terminated with a CR-LF</div><div class="line" id="LC295">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(Carriage Return - Line Feed) pair, and these messages SHALL NOT</div><div class="line" id="LC296">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;exceed 512 characters in length, counting all characters including</div><div class="line" id="LC297">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the trailing CR-LF. Thus, there are 510 characters maximum allowed</div><div class="line" id="LC298">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for the command and its parameters.  There is no provision for</div><div class="line" id="LC299">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continuation of message lines.  See section 6 for more details about</div><div class="line" id="LC300">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;current implementations.</div><div class="line" id="LC301">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC302">2.3.1 Message format in Augmented BNF</div><div class="line" id="LC303">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC304">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The protocol messages must be extracted from the contiguous stream of</div><div class="line" id="LC305">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;octets.  The current solution is to designate two characters, CR and</div><div class="line" id="LC306">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LF, as message separators.  Empty messages are silently ignored,</div><div class="line" id="LC307">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which permits use of the sequence CR-LF between messages without</div><div class="line" id="LC308">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;extra problems.</div><div class="line" id="LC309">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC310">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The extracted message is parsed into the components &lt;prefix&gt;,</div><div class="line" id="LC311">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&lt;command&gt; and list of parameters (&lt;params&gt;).</div><div class="line" id="LC312">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC313">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Augmented BNF representation for this is:</div><div class="line" id="LC314">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC315">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;message    =  [ &quot;:&quot; prefix SPACE ] command [ params ] crlf</div><div class="line" id="LC316">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;prefix     =  servername / ( nickname [ [ &quot;!&quot; user ] &quot;@&quot; host ] )</div><div class="line" id="LC317">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;command    =  1*letter / 3digit</div><div class="line" id="LC318">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;params     =  *14( SPACE middle ) [ SPACE &quot;:&quot; trailing ]</div><div class="line" id="LC319">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;=/ 14( SPACE middle ) [ SPACE [ &quot;:&quot; ] trailing ]</div><div class="line" id="LC320">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC321">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nospcrlfcl =  %x01-09 / %x0B-0C / %x0E-1F / %x21-39 / %x3B-FF</div><div class="line" id="LC322">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; any octet except NUL, CR, LF, &quot; &quot; and &quot;:&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC323">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;middle     =  nospcrlfcl *( &quot;:&quot; / nospcrlfcl )</div><div class="line" id="LC324">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;trailing   =  *( &quot;:&quot; / &quot; &quot; / nospcrlfcl )</div><div class="line" id="LC325">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC326">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;SPACE      =  %x20        ; space character</div><div class="line" id="LC327">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;crlf       =  %x0D %x0A   ; &quot;carriage return&quot; &quot;linefeed&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC328">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC329">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC330">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC331">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC332">Kalt                         Informational                      [Page 6]</div><div class="line" id="LC333">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC334">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC335">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC336">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC337">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;NOTES:</div><div class="line" id="LC338">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1) After extracting the parameter list, all parameters are equal</div><div class="line" id="LC339">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whether matched by &lt;middle&gt; or &lt;trailing&gt;. &lt;trailing&gt; is just a</div><div class="line" id="LC340">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;syntactic trick to allow SPACE within the parameter.</div><div class="line" id="LC341">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC342">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2) The NUL (%x00) character is not special in message framing, and</div><div class="line" id="LC343">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;basically could end up inside a parameter, but it would cause</div><div class="line" id="LC344">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;extra complexities in normal C string handling. Therefore, NUL</div><div class="line" id="LC345">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is not allowed within messages.</div><div class="line" id="LC346">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC347">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Most protocol messages specify additional semantics and syntax for</div><div class="line" id="LC348">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the extracted parameter strings dictated by their position in the</div><div class="line" id="LC349">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;list.  For example, many server commands will assume that the first</div><div class="line" id="LC350">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;parameter after the command is the list of targets, which can be</div><div class="line" id="LC351">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;described with:</div><div class="line" id="LC352">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC353">&nbsp;&nbsp;target     =  nickname / server</div><div class="line" id="LC354">&nbsp;&nbsp;msgtarget  =  msgto *( &quot;,&quot; msgto )</div><div class="line" id="LC355">&nbsp;&nbsp;msgto      =  channel / ( user [ &quot;%&quot; host ] &quot;@&quot; servername )</div><div class="line" id="LC356">&nbsp;&nbsp;msgto      =/ ( user &quot;%&quot; host ) / targetmask</div><div class="line" id="LC357">&nbsp;&nbsp;msgto      =/ nickname / ( nickname &quot;!&quot; user &quot;@&quot; host )</div><div class="line" id="LC358">&nbsp;&nbsp;channel    =  ( &quot;#&quot; / &quot;+&quot; / ( &quot;!&quot; channelid ) / &quot;&amp;&quot; ) chanstring</div><div class="line" id="LC359">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;[ &quot;:&quot; chanstring ]</div><div class="line" id="LC360">&nbsp;&nbsp;servername =  hostname</div><div class="line" id="LC361">&nbsp;&nbsp;host       =  hostname / hostaddr</div><div class="line" id="LC362">&nbsp;&nbsp;hostname   =  shortname *( &quot;.&quot; shortname )</div><div class="line" id="LC363">&nbsp;&nbsp;shortname  =  ( letter / digit ) *( letter / digit / &quot;-&quot; )</div><div class="line" id="LC364">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;*( letter / digit )</div><div class="line" id="LC365">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; as specified in RFC 1123 [HNAME]</div><div class="line" id="LC366">&nbsp;&nbsp;hostaddr   =  ip4addr / ip6addr</div><div class="line" id="LC367">&nbsp;&nbsp;ip4addr    =  1*3digit &quot;.&quot; 1*3digit &quot;.&quot; 1*3digit &quot;.&quot; 1*3digit</div><div class="line" id="LC368">&nbsp;&nbsp;ip6addr    =  1*hexdigit 7( &quot;:&quot; 1*hexdigit )</div><div class="line" id="LC369">&nbsp;&nbsp;ip6addr    =/ &quot;0:0:0:0:0:&quot; ( &quot;0&quot; / &quot;FFFF&quot; ) &quot;:&quot; ip4addr</div><div class="line" id="LC370">&nbsp;&nbsp;nickname   =  ( letter / special ) *8( letter / digit / special / &quot;-&quot; )</div><div class="line" id="LC371">&nbsp;&nbsp;targetmask =  ( &quot;$&quot; / &quot;#&quot; ) mask</div><div class="line" id="LC372">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; see details on allowed masks in section 3.3.1</div><div class="line" id="LC373">&nbsp;&nbsp;chanstring =  %x01-07 / %x08-09 / %x0B-0C / %x0E-1F / %x21-2B</div><div class="line" id="LC374">&nbsp;&nbsp;chanstring =/ %x2D-39 / %x3B-FF</div><div class="line" id="LC375">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; any octet except NUL, BELL, CR, LF, &quot; &quot;, &quot;,&quot; and &quot;:&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC376">&nbsp;&nbsp;channelid  = 5( %x41-5A / digit )   ; 5( A-Z / 0-9 )</div><div class="line" id="LC377">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC378">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC379">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC380">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC381">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC382">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC383">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC384">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC385">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC386">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC387">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC388">Kalt                         Informational                      [Page 7]</div><div class="line" id="LC389">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC390">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC391">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC392">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC393">&nbsp;&nbsp;Other parameter syntaxes are:</div><div class="line" id="LC394">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC395">&nbsp;&nbsp;user       =  1*( %x01-09 / %x0B-0C / %x0E-1F / %x21-3F / %x41-FF )</div><div class="line" id="LC396">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; any octet except NUL, CR, LF, &quot; &quot; and &quot;@&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC397">&nbsp;&nbsp;key        =  1*23( %x01-05 / %x07-08 / %x0C / %x0E-1F / %x21-7F )</div><div class="line" id="LC398">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; any 7-bit US_ASCII character,</div><div class="line" id="LC399">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; except NUL, CR, LF, FF, h/v TABs, and &quot; &quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC400">&nbsp;&nbsp;letter     =  %x41-5A / %x61-7A       ; A-Z / a-z</div><div class="line" id="LC401">&nbsp;&nbsp;digit      =  %x30-39                 ; 0-9</div><div class="line" id="LC402">&nbsp;&nbsp;hexdigit   =  digit / &quot;A&quot; / &quot;B&quot; / &quot;C&quot; / &quot;D&quot; / &quot;E&quot; / &quot;F&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC403">&nbsp;&nbsp;special    =  %x5B-60 / %x7B-7D</div><div class="line" id="LC404">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; &quot;[&quot;, &quot;]&quot;, &quot;\&quot;, &quot;`&quot;, &quot;_&quot;, &quot;^&quot;, &quot;{&quot;, &quot;|&quot;, &quot;}&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC405">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC406">&nbsp;&nbsp;NOTES:</div><div class="line" id="LC407">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1) The &lt;hostaddr&gt; syntax is given here for the sole purpose of</div><div class="line" id="LC408">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;indicating the format to follow for IP addresses.  This</div><div class="line" id="LC409">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;reflects the fact that the only available implementations of</div><div class="line" id="LC410">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;this protocol uses TCP/IP as underlying network protocol but is</div><div class="line" id="LC411">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not meant to prevent other protocols to be used.</div><div class="line" id="LC412">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC413">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2) &lt;hostname&gt; has a maximum length of 63 characters.  This is a</div><div class="line" id="LC414">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;limitation of the protocol as internet hostnames (in</div><div class="line" id="LC415">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;particular) can be longer.  Such restriction is necessary</div><div class="line" id="LC416">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because IRC messages are limited to 512 characters in length.</div><div class="line" id="LC417">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Clients connecting from a host which name is longer than 63</div><div class="line" id="LC418">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;characters are registered using the host (numeric) address</div><div class="line" id="LC419">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;instead of the host name.</div><div class="line" id="LC420">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC421">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3) Some parameters used in the following sections of this</div><div class="line" id="LC422">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;documents are not defined here as there is nothing specific</div><div class="line" id="LC423">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;about them besides the name that is used for convenience.</div><div class="line" id="LC424">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;These parameters follow the general syntax defined for</div><div class="line" id="LC425">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&lt;params&gt;.</div><div class="line" id="LC426">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC427">2.4 Numeric replies</div><div class="line" id="LC428">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC429">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Most of the messages sent to the server generate a reply of some</div><div class="line" id="LC430">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sort.  The most common reply is the numeric reply, used for both</div><div class="line" id="LC431">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;errors and normal replies.  The numeric reply MUST be sent as one</div><div class="line" id="LC432">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;message consisting of the sender prefix, the three-digit numeric, and</div><div class="line" id="LC433">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the target of the reply.  A numeric reply is not allowed to originate</div><div class="line" id="LC434">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from a client. In all other respects, a numeric reply is just like a</div><div class="line" id="LC435">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;normal message, except that the keyword is made up of 3 numeric</div><div class="line" id="LC436">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;digits rather than a string of letters.  A list of different replies</div><div class="line" id="LC437">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is supplied in section 5 (Replies).</div><div class="line" id="LC438">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC439">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC440">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC441">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC442">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC443">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC444">Kalt                         Informational                      [Page 8]</div><div class="line" id="LC445">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC446">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC447">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC448">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC449">2.5 Wildcard expressions</div><div class="line" id="LC450">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC451">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When wildcards are allowed in a string, it is referred as a &quot;mask&quot;.</div><div class="line" id="LC452">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC453">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For string matching purposes, the protocol allows the use of two</div><div class="line" id="LC454">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;special characters: &#39;?&#39; (%x3F) to match one and only one character,</div><div class="line" id="LC455">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and &#39;*&#39; (%x2A) to match any number of any characters.  These two</div><div class="line" id="LC456">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;characters can be escaped using the character &#39;\&#39; (%x5C).</div><div class="line" id="LC457">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC458">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Augmented BNF syntax for this is:</div><div class="line" id="LC459">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC460">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mask       =  *( nowild / noesc wildone / noesc wildmany )</div><div class="line" id="LC461">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wildone    =  %x3F</div><div class="line" id="LC462">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wildmany   =  %x2A</div><div class="line" id="LC463">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nowild     =  %x01-29 / %x2B-3E / %x40-FF</div><div class="line" id="LC464">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; any octet except NUL, &quot;*&quot;, &quot;?&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC465">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;noesc      =  %x01-5B / %x5D-FF</div><div class="line" id="LC466">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; any octet except NUL and &quot;\&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC467">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;matchone   =  %x01-FF</div><div class="line" id="LC468">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; matches wildone</div><div class="line" id="LC469">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;matchmany  =  *matchone</div><div class="line" id="LC470">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; matches wildmany</div><div class="line" id="LC471">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC472">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Examples:</div><div class="line" id="LC473">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC474">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a?c         ; Matches any string of 3 characters in length starting</div><div class="line" id="LC475">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with &quot;a&quot; and ending with &quot;c&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC476">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC477">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a*c         ; Matches any string of at least 2 characters in length</div><div class="line" id="LC478">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;starting with &quot;a&quot; and ending with &quot;c&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC479">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC480">3. Message Details</div><div class="line" id="LC481">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC482">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On the following pages there are descriptions of each message</div><div class="line" id="LC483">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;recognized by the IRC server and client.  All commands described in</div><div class="line" id="LC484">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;this section MUST be implemented by any server for this protocol.</div><div class="line" id="LC485">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC486">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Where the reply ERR_NOSUCHSERVER is returned, it means that the</div><div class="line" id="LC487">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;target of the message could not be found.  The server MUST NOT send</div><div class="line" id="LC488">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;any other replies after this error for that command.</div><div class="line" id="LC489">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC490">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The server to which a client is connected is required to parse the</div><div class="line" id="LC491">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;complete message, and return any appropriate errors.</div><div class="line" id="LC492">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC493">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;If multiple parameters is presented, then each MUST be checked for</div><div class="line" id="LC494">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;validity and appropriate responses MUST be sent back to the client.</div><div class="line" id="LC495">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In the case of incorrect messages which use parameter lists with</div><div class="line" id="LC496">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;comma as an item separator, a reply MUST be sent for each item.</div><div class="line" id="LC497">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC498">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC499">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC500">Kalt                         Informational                      [Page 9]</div><div class="line" id="LC501">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC502">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC503">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC504">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC505">3.1 Connection Registration</div><div class="line" id="LC506">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC507">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The commands described here are used to register a connection with an</div><div class="line" id="LC508">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;IRC server as a user as well as to correctly disconnect.</div><div class="line" id="LC509">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC510">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A &quot;PASS&quot; command is not required for a client connection to be</div><div class="line" id="LC511">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;registered, but it MUST precede the latter of the NICK/USER</div><div class="line" id="LC512">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;combination (for a user connection) or the SERVICE command (for a</div><div class="line" id="LC513">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;service connection). The RECOMMENDED order for a client to register</div><div class="line" id="LC514">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is as follows:</div><div class="line" id="LC515">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC516">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1. Pass message</div><div class="line" id="LC517">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2. Nick message                 2. Service message</div><div class="line" id="LC518">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3. User message</div><div class="line" id="LC519">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC520">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Upon success, the client will receive an RPL_WELCOME (for users) or</div><div class="line" id="LC521">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;RPL_YOURESERVICE (for services) message indicating that the</div><div class="line" id="LC522">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;connection is now registered and known the to the entire IRC network.</div><div class="line" id="LC523">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The reply message MUST contain the full client identifier upon which</div><div class="line" id="LC524">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it was registered.</div><div class="line" id="LC525">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC526">3.1.1 Password message</div><div class="line" id="LC527">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC528">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Command: PASS</div><div class="line" id="LC529">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Parameters: &lt;password&gt;</div><div class="line" id="LC530">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC531">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The PASS command is used to set a &#39;connection password&#39;.  The</div><div class="line" id="LC532">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;optional password can and MUST be set before any attempt to register</div><div class="line" id="LC533">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the connection is made.  Currently this requires that user send a</div><div class="line" id="LC534">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;PASS command before sending the NICK/USER combination.</div><div class="line" id="LC535">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC536">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Numeric Replies:</div><div class="line" id="LC537">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC538">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_NEEDMOREPARAMS              ERR_ALREADYREGISTRED</div><div class="line" id="LC539">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC540">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Example:</div><div class="line" id="LC541">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC542">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;PASS secretpasswordhere</div><div class="line" id="LC543">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC544">3.1.2 Nick message</div><div class="line" id="LC545">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC546">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC547">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Command: NICK</div><div class="line" id="LC548">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Parameters: &lt;nickname&gt;</div><div class="line" id="LC549">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC550">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;NICK command is used to give user a nickname or change the existing</div><div class="line" id="LC551">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;one.</div><div class="line" id="LC552">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC553">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC554">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC555">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC556">Kalt                         Informational                     [Page 10]</div><div class="line" id="LC557">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC558">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC559">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC560">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC561">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Numeric Replies:</div><div class="line" id="LC562">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC563">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_NONICKNAMEGIVEN             ERR_ERRONEUSNICKNAME</div><div class="line" id="LC564">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_NICKNAMEINUSE               ERR_NICKCOLLISION</div><div class="line" id="LC565">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_UNAVAILRESOURCE             ERR_RESTRICTED</div><div class="line" id="LC566">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC567">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Examples:</div><div class="line" id="LC568">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC569">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;NICK Wiz                ; Introducing new nick &quot;Wiz&quot; if session is</div><div class="line" id="LC570">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;still unregistered, or user changing his</div><div class="line" id="LC571">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nickname to &quot;Wiz&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC572">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC573">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;:WiZ!jto@tolsun.oulu.fi NICK Kilroy</div><div class="line" id="LC574">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;; Server telling that WiZ changed his</div><div class="line" id="LC575">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nickname to Kilroy.</div><div class="line" id="LC576">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC577">3.1.3 User message</div><div class="line" id="LC578">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC579">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Command: USER</div><div class="line" id="LC580">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Parameters: &lt;user&gt; &lt;mode&gt; &lt;unused&gt; &lt;realname&gt;</div><div class="line" id="LC581">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC582">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The USER command is used at the beginning of connection to specify</div><div class="line" id="LC583">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the username, hostname and realname of a new user.</div><div class="line" id="LC584">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC585">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The &lt;mode&gt; parameter should be a numeric, and can be used to</div><div class="line" id="LC586">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;automatically set user modes when registering with the server.  This</div><div class="line" id="LC587">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;parameter is a bitmask, with only 2 bits having any signification: if</div><div class="line" id="LC588">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the bit 2 is set, the user mode &#39;w&#39; will be set and if the bit 3 is</div><div class="line" id="LC589">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;set, the user mode &#39;i&#39; will be set.  (See Section 3.1.5 &quot;User</div><div class="line" id="LC590">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Modes&quot;).</div><div class="line" id="LC591">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC592">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The &lt;realname&gt; may contain space characters.</div><div class="line" id="LC593">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC594">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Numeric Replies:</div><div class="line" id="LC595">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC596">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_NEEDMOREPARAMS              ERR_ALREADYREGISTRED</div><div class="line" id="LC597">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC598">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Example:</div><div class="line" id="LC599">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC600">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;USER guest 0 * :Ronnie Reagan   ; User registering themselves with a</div><div class="line" id="LC601">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;username of &quot;guest&quot; and real name</div><div class="line" id="LC602">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&quot;Ronnie Reagan&quot;.</div><div class="line" id="LC603">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC604">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;USER guest 8 * :Ronnie Reagan   ; User registering themselves with a</div><div class="line" id="LC605">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;username of &quot;guest&quot; and real name</div><div class="line" id="LC606">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&quot;Ronnie Reagan&quot;, and asking to be set</div><div class="line" id="LC607">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;invisible.</div><div class="line" id="LC608">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC609">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC610">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC611">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC612">Kalt                         Informational                     [Page 11]</div><div class="line" id="LC613">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC614">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC615">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC616">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC617">3.1.4 Oper message</div><div class="line" id="LC618">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC619">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Command: OPER</div><div class="line" id="LC620">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Parameters: &lt;name&gt; &lt;password&gt;</div><div class="line" id="LC621">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC622">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A normal user uses the OPER command to obtain operator privileges.</div><div class="line" id="LC623">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The combination of &lt;name&gt; and &lt;password&gt; are REQUIRED to gain</div><div class="line" id="LC624">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Operator privileges.  Upon success, the user will receive a MODE</div><div class="line" id="LC625">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;message (see section 3.1.5) indicating the new user modes.</div><div class="line" id="LC626">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC627">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Numeric Replies:</div><div class="line" id="LC628">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC629">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_NEEDMOREPARAMS              RPL_YOUREOPER</div><div class="line" id="LC630">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_NOOPERHOST                  ERR_PASSWDMISMATCH</div><div class="line" id="LC631">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC632">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Example:</div><div class="line" id="LC633">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC634">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;OPER foo bar                    ; Attempt to register as an operator</div><div class="line" id="LC635">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;using a username of &quot;foo&quot; and &quot;bar&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC636">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as the password.</div><div class="line" id="LC637">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC638">3.1.5 User mode message</div><div class="line" id="LC639">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC640">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Command: MODE</div><div class="line" id="LC641">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Parameters: &lt;nickname&gt;</div><div class="line" id="LC642">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;*( ( &quot;+&quot; / &quot;-&quot; ) *( &quot;i&quot; / &quot;w&quot; / &quot;o&quot; / &quot;O&quot; / &quot;r&quot; ) )</div><div class="line" id="LC643">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC644">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The user MODE&#39;s are typically changes which affect either how the</div><div class="line" id="LC645">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;client is seen by others or what &#39;extra&#39; messages the client is sent.</div><div class="line" id="LC646">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC647">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A user MODE command MUST only be accepted if both the sender of the</div><div class="line" id="LC648">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;message and the nickname given as a parameter are both the same.  If</div><div class="line" id="LC649">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no other parameter is given, then the server will return the current</div><div class="line" id="LC650">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;settings for the nick.</div><div class="line" id="LC651">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC652">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The available modes are as follows:</div><div class="line" id="LC653">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC654">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a - user is flagged as away;</div><div class="line" id="LC655">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;i - marks a users as invisible;</div><div class="line" id="LC656">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;w - user receives wallops;</div><div class="line" id="LC657">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;r - restricted user connection;</div><div class="line" id="LC658">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;o - operator flag;</div><div class="line" id="LC659">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O - local operator flag;</div><div class="line" id="LC660">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;s - marks a user for receipt of server notices.</div><div class="line" id="LC661">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC662">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Additional modes may be available later on.</div><div class="line" id="LC663">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC664">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC665">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC666">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC667">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC668">Kalt                         Informational                     [Page 12]</div><div class="line" id="LC669">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC670">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC671">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC672">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC673">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The flag &#39;a&#39; SHALL NOT be toggled by the user using the MODE command,</div><div class="line" id="LC674">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;instead use of the AWAY command is REQUIRED.</div><div class="line" id="LC675">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC676">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;If a user attempts to make themselves an operator using the &quot;+o&quot; or</div><div class="line" id="LC677">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&quot;+O&quot; flag, the attempt SHOULD be ignored as users could bypass the</div><div class="line" id="LC678">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;authentication mechanisms of the OPER command.  There is no</div><div class="line" id="LC679">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;restriction, however, on anyone `deopping&#39; themselves (using &quot;-o&quot; or</div><div class="line" id="LC680">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&quot;-O&quot;).</div><div class="line" id="LC681">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC682">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On the other hand, if a user attempts to make themselves unrestricted</div><div class="line" id="LC683">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;using the &quot;-r&quot; flag, the attempt SHOULD be ignored.  There is no</div><div class="line" id="LC684">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;restriction, however, on anyone `deopping&#39; themselves (using &quot;+r&quot;).</div><div class="line" id="LC685">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This flag is typically set by the server upon connection for</div><div class="line" id="LC686">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;administrative reasons.  While the restrictions imposed are left up</div><div class="line" id="LC687">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to the implementation, it is typical that a restricted user not be</div><div class="line" id="LC688">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;allowed to change nicknames, nor make use of the channel operator</div><div class="line" id="LC689">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;status on channels.</div><div class="line" id="LC690">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC691">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The flag &#39;s&#39; is obsolete but MAY still be used.</div><div class="line" id="LC692">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC693">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Numeric Replies:</div><div class="line" id="LC694">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC695">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_NEEDMOREPARAMS              ERR_USERSDONTMATCH</div><div class="line" id="LC696">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_UMODEUNKNOWNFLAG            RPL_UMODEIS</div><div class="line" id="LC697">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC698">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Examples:</div><div class="line" id="LC699">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC700">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;MODE WiZ -w                     ; Command by WiZ to turn off</div><div class="line" id="LC701">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;reception of WALLOPS messages.</div><div class="line" id="LC702">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC703">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;MODE Angel +i                   ; Command from Angel to make herself</div><div class="line" id="LC704">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;invisible.</div><div class="line" id="LC705">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC706">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;MODE WiZ -o                     ; WiZ &#39;deopping&#39; (removing operator</div><div class="line" id="LC707">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;status).</div><div class="line" id="LC708">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC709">3.1.6 Service message</div><div class="line" id="LC710">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC711">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Command: SERVICE</div><div class="line" id="LC712">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Parameters: &lt;nickname&gt; &lt;reserved&gt; &lt;distribution&gt; &lt;type&gt;</div><div class="line" id="LC713">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&lt;reserved&gt; &lt;info&gt;</div><div class="line" id="LC714">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC715">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The SERVICE command to register a new service.  Command parameters</div><div class="line" id="LC716">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;specify the service nickname, distribution, type and info of a new</div><div class="line" id="LC717">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;service.</div><div class="line" id="LC718">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC719">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC720">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC721">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC722">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC723">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC724">Kalt                         Informational                     [Page 13]</div><div class="line" id="LC725">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC726">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC727">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC728">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC729">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The &lt;distribution&gt; parameter is used to specify the visibility of a</div><div class="line" id="LC730">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;service.  The service may only be known to servers which have a name</div><div class="line" id="LC731">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;matching the distribution.  For a matching server to have knowledge</div><div class="line" id="LC732">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of the service, the network path between that server and the server</div><div class="line" id="LC733">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on which the service is connected MUST be composed of servers which</div><div class="line" id="LC734">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;names all match the mask.</div><div class="line" id="LC735">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC736">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The &lt;type&gt; parameter is currently reserved for future usage.</div><div class="line" id="LC737">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC738">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Numeric Replies:</div><div class="line" id="LC739">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC740">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_ALREADYREGISTRED            ERR_NEEDMOREPARAMS</div><div class="line" id="LC741">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_ERRONEUSNICKNAME</div><div class="line" id="LC742">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;RPL_YOURESERVICE                RPL_YOURHOST</div><div class="line" id="LC743">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;RPL_MYINFO</div><div class="line" id="LC744">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC745">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Example:</div><div class="line" id="LC746">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC747">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;SERVICE dict * *.fr 0 0 :French Dictionary ; Service registering</div><div class="line" id="LC748">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;itself with a name of &quot;dict&quot;.  This</div><div class="line" id="LC749">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;service will only be available on</div><div class="line" id="LC750">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;servers which name matches &quot;*.fr&quot;.</div><div class="line" id="LC751">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC752">3.1.7 Quit</div><div class="line" id="LC753">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC754">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Command: QUIT</div><div class="line" id="LC755">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Parameters: [ &lt;Quit Message&gt; ]</div><div class="line" id="LC756">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC757">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A client session is terminated with a quit message.  The server</div><div class="line" id="LC758">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;acknowledges this by sending an ERROR message to the client.</div><div class="line" id="LC759">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC760">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Numeric Replies:</div><div class="line" id="LC761">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC762">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;None.</div><div class="line" id="LC763">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC764">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Example:</div><div class="line" id="LC765">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC766">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;QUIT :Gone to have lunch        ; Preferred message format.</div><div class="line" id="LC767">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC768">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;:syrk!kalt@millennium.stealth.net QUIT :Gone to have lunch ; User</div><div class="line" id="LC769">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;syrk has quit IRC to have lunch.</div><div class="line" id="LC770">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC771">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC772">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC773">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC774">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC775">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC776">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC777">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC778">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC779">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC780">Kalt                         Informational                     [Page 14]</div><div class="line" id="LC781">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC782">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC783">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC784">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC785">3.1.8 Squit</div><div class="line" id="LC786">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC787">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Command: SQUIT</div><div class="line" id="LC788">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Parameters: &lt;server&gt; &lt;comment&gt;</div><div class="line" id="LC789">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC790">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The SQUIT command is available only to operators.  It is used to</div><div class="line" id="LC791">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;disconnect server links.  Also servers can generate SQUIT messages on</div><div class="line" id="LC792">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;error conditions.  A SQUIT message may also target a remote server</div><div class="line" id="LC793">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;connection.  In this case, the SQUIT message will simply be sent to</div><div class="line" id="LC794">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the remote server without affecting the servers in between the</div><div class="line" id="LC795">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;operator and the remote server.</div><div class="line" id="LC796">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC797">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The &lt;comment&gt; SHOULD be supplied by all operators who execute a SQUIT</div><div class="line" id="LC798">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for a remote server.  The server ordered to disconnect its peer</div><div class="line" id="LC799">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;generates a WALLOPS message with &lt;comment&gt; included, so that other</div><div class="line" id="LC800">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;users may be aware of the reason of this action.</div><div class="line" id="LC801">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC802">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Numeric replies:</div><div class="line" id="LC803">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC804">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_NOPRIVILEGES                ERR_NOSUCHSERVER</div><div class="line" id="LC805">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_NEEDMOREPARAMS</div><div class="line" id="LC806">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC807">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Examples:</div><div class="line" id="LC808">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC809">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;SQUIT tolsun.oulu.fi :Bad Link ?  ; Command to uplink of the server</div><div class="line" id="LC810">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;tolson.oulu.fi to terminate its</div><div class="line" id="LC811">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;connection with comment &quot;Bad Link&quot;.</div><div class="line" id="LC812">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC813">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;:Trillian SQUIT cm22.eng.umd.edu :Server out of control ; Command</div><div class="line" id="LC814">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from Trillian from to disconnect</div><div class="line" id="LC815">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&quot;cm22.eng.umd.edu&quot; from the net with</div><div class="line" id="LC816">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;comment &quot;Server out of control&quot;.</div><div class="line" id="LC817">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC818">3.2 Channel operations</div><div class="line" id="LC819">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC820">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This group of messages is concerned with manipulating channels, their</div><div class="line" id="LC821">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;properties (channel modes), and their contents (typically users).</div><div class="line" id="LC822">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For this reason, these messages SHALL NOT be made available to</div><div class="line" id="LC823">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;services.</div><div class="line" id="LC824">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC825">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;All of these messages are requests which will or will not be granted</div><div class="line" id="LC826">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by the server.  The server MUST send a reply informing the user</div><div class="line" id="LC827">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whether the request was granted, denied or generated an error.  When</div><div class="line" id="LC828">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the server grants the request, the message is typically sent back</div><div class="line" id="LC829">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(eventually reformatted) to the user with the prefix set to the user</div><div class="line" id="LC830">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;itself.</div><div class="line" id="LC831">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC832">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC833">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC834">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC835">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC836">Kalt                         Informational                     [Page 15]</div><div class="line" id="LC837">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC838">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC839">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC840">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC841">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The rules governing how channels are managed are enforced by the</div><div class="line" id="LC842">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;servers.  These rules are beyond the scope of this document.  More</div><div class="line" id="LC843">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;details are found in &quot;Internet Relay Chat: Channel Management&quot; [IRC-</div><div class="line" id="LC844">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;CHAN].</div><div class="line" id="LC845">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC846">3.2.1 Join message</div><div class="line" id="LC847">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC848">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Command: JOIN</div><div class="line" id="LC849">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Parameters: ( &lt;channel&gt; *( &quot;,&quot; &lt;channel&gt; ) [ &lt;key&gt; *( &quot;,&quot; &lt;key&gt; ) ] )</div><div class="line" id="LC850">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;/ &quot;0&quot;</div><div class="line" id="LC851">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC852">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The JOIN command is used by a user to request to start listening to</div><div class="line" id="LC853">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the specific channel.  Servers MUST be able to parse arguments in the</div><div class="line" id="LC854">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;form of a list of target, but SHOULD NOT use lists when sending JOIN</div><div class="line" id="LC855">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;messages to clients.</div><div class="line" id="LC856">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC857">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Once a user has joined a channel, he receives information about</div><div class="line" id="LC858">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all commands his server receives affecting the channel.  This</div><div class="line" id="LC859">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;includes JOIN, MODE, KICK, PART, QUIT and of course PRIVMSG/NOTICE.</div><div class="line" id="LC860">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This allows channel members to keep track of the other channel</div><div class="line" id="LC861">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;members, as well as channel modes.</div><div class="line" id="LC862">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC863">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;If a JOIN is successful, the user receives a JOIN message as</div><div class="line" id="LC864">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;confirmation and is then sent the channel&#39;s topic (using RPL_TOPIC) and</div><div class="line" id="LC865">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the list of users who are on the channel (using RPL_NAMREPLY), which</div><div class="line" id="LC866">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;MUST include the user joining.</div><div class="line" id="LC867">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC868">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Note that this message accepts a special argument (&quot;0&quot;), which is</div><div class="line" id="LC869">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a special request to leave all channels the user is currently a member</div><div class="line" id="LC870">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of.  The server will process this message as if the user had sent</div><div class="line" id="LC871">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a PART command (See Section 3.2.2) for each channel he is a member</div><div class="line" id="LC872">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of.</div><div class="line" id="LC873">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC874">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Numeric Replies:</div><div class="line" id="LC875">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC876">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_NEEDMOREPARAMS              ERR_BANNEDFROMCHAN</div><div class="line" id="LC877">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_INVITEONLYCHAN              ERR_BADCHANNELKEY</div><div class="line" id="LC878">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_CHANNELISFULL               ERR_BADCHANMASK</div><div class="line" id="LC879">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_NOSUCHCHANNEL               ERR_TOOMANYCHANNELS</div><div class="line" id="LC880">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ERR_TOOMANYTARGETS              ERR_UNAVAILRESOURCE</div><div class="line" id="LC881">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;RPL_TOPIC</div><div class="line" id="LC882">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC883">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Examples:</div><div class="line" id="LC884">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC885">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;JOIN #foobar                    ; Command to join channel #foobar.</div><div class="line" id="LC886">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC887">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;JOIN &amp;foo fubar                 ; Command to join channel &amp;foo using</div><div class="line" id="LC888">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;key &quot;fubar&quot;.</div><div class="line" id="LC889">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC890">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC891">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC892">Kalt                         Informational                     [Page 16]</div><div class="line" id="LC893">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC894">RFC 2812          Internet Relay Chat: Client Protocol        April 2000</div><div class="line" id="LC895">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC896">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC897">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;JOIN #foo,&amp;bar fubar            ; Command to join channel #foo using</div><div class="line" id="LC898">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;key &quot;fubar&quot; and &amp;bar using no key.</div><div class="line" id="LC899">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC900">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;JOIN #foo,#bar fubar,foobar     ; Command to join channel #foo using</div><div class="line" id="LC901">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;key &quot;fubar&quot;, and channel #bar using</div><div class="line" id="LC902">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;key &quot;foobar&quot;.</div><div class="line" id="LC903">&nbsp;</div><div class="line" id="LC904">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;JOIN #foo,#bar                  ;
